}

class="m-detail-header--aspect-ratio-wrapper"><div class="m-detail-header--aspect-ratio-pusher"></div></div></phoenix-picture><div class="m-detail-header--content"><dl><dt class="m-detail-header--date m-detail-header--updated-date-term m-detail-header--meta-item">Updated:</dt><dd class="m-detail-header--date m-detail-header--updated-date-definition"><phoenix-timeago><time datetime="2018-08-22T23:49:17-04:00" title="Aug 22, 2018">Aug 22, 2018</time></phoenix-timeago></dd><dt class="m-detail-header--date m-detail-header--updated-date-term m-detail-header--meta-item">Original:</dt><dd class="m-detail-header--date m-detail-header--updated-date-definition"><phoenix-timeago><time datetime="2016-08-30T12:15:36-04:00" title="Aug 30, 2016">Aug 30, 2016</time></phoenix-timeago></dd></dl><h1 class="m-detail-header--title">Did Lucy, Famed Human Ancestor, Die After Falling From a Tree?</h1><div class="m-detail-header--dek">In a new study, researchers claim to have solved the mystery of how the early human ancestor known as Lucy died nearly 3.2 million years ago.
</div><div class="m-detail-header--meta"><dl><dt>Author:</dt><dd class="m-detail-header--meta-item"><a class="m-detail-header--meta-author" href="/author/sarah-pruitt" onclick="return phoenixTrackClickEvent(this, event);" phx-track-id="Author Name" rel="author">Sarah Pruitt</a></dd></dl></div></div></div></header><div class="m-detail--contents l-content-well"><section class="l-grid lm-grid--detail lm-grid--with-right-rail"><div class="l-grid--content-body"><header class="m-detail-header mm-detail-header--featured mm-detail-header--in-content-well"><div class="m-detail-header--container"><div class="m-detail-header--content"><div class="m-detail-header--dek">In a new study, researchers claim to have solved the mystery of how the early human ancestor known as Lucy died nearly 3.2 million years ago.
</div></div></div></header><section class="m-social mm-social--below-header"><ul><li class="m-social--facebook"><a class="m-icon-button m-social--button" aria-label="facebook" rel="noopener" xlink:href="/assets-global/icons/svg-sprite.svg?v=2021-03-31-150456-c8a52d4-019516#ico_pinterest"></use></svg></phoenix-icon-fallback></a></li><li class="m-social--print"><a class="m-icon-button xlink:href="/assets-global/icons/svg-sprite.svg?v=2021-03-31-150456-c8a52d4-019516#ico_print"></use></svg></phoenix-icon-fallback></a></li></ul></section><div class="m-detail--sponsor"></div><div class="m-detail--body"><!-- tml-version="2" --><p>The discovery of Lucy&#x2019;s partial skeleton represented a major breakthrough in the study of ancient human ancestors, enabling scientists to establish that early hominids like Australopithecus afarensis learned to walk upright before their brains grew larger. Though Lucy&#x2019;s feet, knees and hips resembled those of modern humans, she had a small head, with a brain similar in size to that of a chimpanzee. Also like chimps, early hominids matured at an earlier age than modern humans: Lucy&#x2019;s skeleton and teeth show that she had reached maturity even though she was only around 15 or 16 years old when she died. She measured 3 feet 6 inches tall and weighed 60 pounds.</p><aside class="m-in-content-ad-row l-inline not-size-b not-size-c not-size-d"><div class="m-header-ad not-size-b not-size-c not-size-d" data-class-rules="[]" data-ad-group="header-0"><div class="m-header-ad--slot is-placeholder not-size-b not-size-c not-size-d"><div id="ad-05727f1c3ee74daa93f9559b7529545d"></div></div></div></aside><p>The new study, <a href="http://www.nature.com/nature/journal/vaop/ncurrent/full/nature19332.html" rel="noopener" onclick="return phoenixTrackClickEvent(this, event);" target="_blank">published</a> this week in the journal Nature, originated in the mid-2000s, when Lucy&#x2019;s skeleton was on temporary loan from the National Museum of Ethiopia for a traveling exhibition in the United States. After a show at the Houston Museum of Natural Science, researchers at the University of Texas at Austin spent 10 days examining the famous fossil&#x2014;which includes bones from the skull, upper limb, hand, axial skeleton, pelvis, lower limb and foot&#x2014;using high-resolution, high-energy Computed Tomography (CT) scanning equipment.</p><aside class="m-in-content-ad-row l-inline not-size-b not-size-c not-size-d"><div class="m-in-content-ad not-size-b not-size-c not-size-d" data-class-rules="[{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;0x0&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;m-advertisement--fluid-card&quot;]}]" data-ad-group="in_content-0"><div class="m-in-content-ad--slot is-placeholder not-size-b not-size-c not-size-d"><div id="ad-a58e4eb28e454a51b9d847563b3d7edd"></div></div></div></aside><div class="m-detail--body-item m-detail--body-item-inline"><figure class="l-inline tml-image m-detail--tml-image--inline" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject"><phoenix-picture><a><picture class="is-waiting-to-load"><source type="image/webp" sizes="(min-width: 334px) 334px, calc(100vw - 40px)" data-srcset="https://www.history.com/.image/c_limit%2Ccs_srgb%2Cq_auto:good%2Cw_334/MTU3ODc4NjAzNTE0OTE0NTI3/image-placeholder-title.webp 334w"><source sizes="(min-width: 334px) 334px, calc(100vw - 40px)" data-srcset="https://www.history.com/.image/c_limit%2Ccs_srgb%2Cfl_progressive%2Cq_auto:good%2Cw_334/MTU3ODc4NjAzNTE0OTE0NTI3/image-placeholder-title.jpg 334w"><img class="m-detail--tml-image m-image" alt="Model of the early hominin Lucy. (Credit: Sch&#xF6;ning / ullstein bild / Getty Images)" decoding="async" src="https://www.history.com/.image/t_share/MTU3ODc4NjAzNTE0OTE0NTI3/image-placeholder-title.jpg" data-src="https://www.history.com/.image/c_limit%2Ccs_srgb%2Cfl_progressive%2Cq_auto:good%2Cw_700/MTU3ODc4NjAzNTE0OTE0NTI3/image-placeholder-title.jpg" height="250" width="334" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" itemprop="contentUrl url"></picture></a><div class="m-detail--tml-image-wrapper" style="max-width:334px; min-width:0px;"><div class="m-detail--tml-image-container" style="padding-top: 75%"><button class="m-social--pinterest-pin-it" onclick="javascript:window.open(&apos;https://www.pinterest.com/pin/create/button/?url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.history.com%2Fnews%2Fdid-lucy-famed-human-ancestor-die-after-falling-from-a-tree&amp;media=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.history.com%2F.image%2Ft_share%2FMTU3ODc4NjAzNTE0OTE0NTI3%2Fimage-placeholder-title.jpg&apos;,&apos;pin&apos;+new Date().getTime(),&apos;status=no,resizable=yes,scrollbars=yes,personalbar=no,directories=no,location=no,toolbar=no,menubar=no,width=632,height=270,left=0,top=0&apos;);"><phoenix-icon-fallback class="m-svg" icon="pinterest-pin-it"><svg><use xlink:href="/assets-global/icons/svg-sprite.svg?v=2021-03-31-150456-c8a52d4-019516#pinterest-pin-it"/></svg></phoenix-icon-fallback></button></div></div></phoenix-picture><figcaption><p class="tml-image--caption" itemprop="caption">Model of the early hominin Lucy. (Credit: Sch&#xF6;ning / ullstein bild / Getty Images)</p></figcaption></figure></div><p>According to John Kappelman, a professor of anthropology at UT Austin who is the lead author of the new study, analysis of the scans revealed puzzling fractures in the upper arm and shoulders, with no signs of healing&#x2014;indicating that the injuries may have occurred around the time of Lucy&#x2019;s death. Kappelman and his colleagues consulted with orthopedic surgeons, who confirmed that the break in Lucy&#x2019;s upper right arm appeared to be a compressive fracture, which can occur when someone falls from a great height.</p><aside class="m-in-content-ad-row l-inline not-size-a not-size-b"><div class="m-in-content-ad not-size-a not-size-b" data-class-rules="[{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;728x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-728x90&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;0x0&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;m-advertisement--fluid-card&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x90&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x250&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x250&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x90&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x250&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x250&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x90&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x250&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x250&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x90&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x250&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x250&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x90&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x250&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x250&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x90&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x250&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x250&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x90&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x250&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x250&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x90&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x250&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x250&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x90&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x250&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x250&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x90&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x250&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x250&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x90 data-ad-group="in_content-0"><div class="m-in-content-ad--slot is-placeholder not-size-a not-size-b"><div id="ad-d23d96e5d1b840b391520257006c5f6c"></div></div></div></aside><aside class="m-in-content-ad-row l-inline not-size-a not-size-c not-size-d"><div class="m-in-content-ad not-size-a not-size-c not-size-d" data-class-rules="[{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;728x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-728x90&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x90&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;0x0&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;m-advertisement--fluid-card&quot;]}]" data-ad-group="in_content-0"><div class="m-in-content-ad--slot is-placeholder not-size-a not-size-c not-size-d"><div id="ad-a9f2cb58b88d4f98ad48dfa4aa078f28"></div></div></div></aside><aside class="m-in-content-ad-row l-inline not-size-b not-size-c not-size-d"><div class="m-in-content-ad not-size-b not-size-c not-size-d" data-class-rules="[{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;0x0&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;m-advertisement--fluid-card&quot;]}]" data-ad-group="in_content-1"><div class="m-in-content-ad--slot is-placeholder not-size-b not-size-c not-size-d"><div id="ad-5d0b42318bc94b76ab7287444eaeccc1"></div></div></div></aside><p>With this in mind, the researchers inspected the rest of Lucy&#x2019;s skeleton&#x2014;including virtual 3D models they made from the scans as well as the original bones in Ethiopia&#x2014;looking for other fractures that could have been caused by a fall. Though they found numerous breaks that likely occurred after she died (as the bones aged and were buried by sand), they also found more compression fractures and other breaks that appear to have been caused by a fall.</p><p>In the new study&#x2019;s version of events, Lucy died quickly but not painlessly. The researchers believe she fell from a height of some 40 feet, hitting the ground at a speed of more than 35 mph. Because the area in which Lucy&#x2019;s skeleton was found was low-lying, with no cliffs nearby, they believe she must have fallen from a tree. From the pattern of breaks in Lucy&#x2019;s ankles, knees, hips and shoulders, the scientists hypothesized that she hit the ground feet first. Both of her shoulders were fractured in a way that suggests she stretched out her arms to break her fall, indicating she was conscious at the time of her death. But, the study&#x2019;s authors concluded, &#x201C;death followed swiftly&#x201D; after the fall, as she likely suffered extensive injuries to her internal organs in addition to the broken bones.</p><p>&#x201C;By understanding her death is how [Lucy] came alive to me,&#x201D; Kappelman <a href="http://www.usatoday.com/story/tech/sciencefair/2016/08/29/lucy-fossil-death-tree-ethiopia/89509676/" rel="noopener" onclick="return phoenixTrackClickEvent(this, event);" target="_blank">told</a> USA Today. &#x201C;Lucy was no longer simply a box of bones but in death became a real individual: a small, broken body lying helpless at the bottom of a tree.&#x201D; He and his colleagues also explored alternate hypotheses about Lucy&#x2019;s cause of death, including a flood, a seizure, a lightning strike or attack by an animal, but none matched with the pattern of fractures they found.</p><aside class="m-in-content-ad-row l-inline not-size-a not-size-b"><div class="m-in-content-ad not-size-a not-size-b" data-ad-group="in_content-1"><div class="m-in-content-ad--slot is-placeholder not-size-a not-size-b"><div id="ad-c19c6309d8d04b9a8f1ee9e80934d2cf"></div></div></div></aside><aside class="m-in-content-ad-row l-inline not-size-a not-size-c not-size-d"><div class="m-in-content-ad not-size-a not-size-c not-size-d" data-class-rules="[{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;728x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-728x90&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;970x90&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;is-970x90&quot;]},{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;0x0&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;m-advertisement--fluid-card&quot;]}]" data-ad-group="in_content-1"><div class="m-in-content-ad--slot is-placeholder not-size-a not-size-c not-size-d"><div id="ad-02aabaad0cfc48e58c50e32458ae7636"></div></div></div></aside><aside class="m-in-content-ad-row l-inline not-size-b not-size-c not-size-d"><div class="m-in-content-ad not-size-b not-size-c not-size-d" data-class-rules="[{&quot;sizes&quot;:[&quot;0x0&quot;],&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;m-advertisement--fluid-card&quot;]}]" data-ad-group="in_content-2"><div class="m-in-content-ad--slot is-placeholder not-size-b not-size-c not-size-d"><div id="ad-46d47a7ce44c412e8122df24c62c3ff0"></div></div></div></aside><div class="m-detail--body-item m-detail--body-item-inline"><figure class="l-inline tml-image m-detail--tml-image--inline" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject"><phoenix-picture><a><picture class="is-waiting-to-load"><source type="image/webp" sizes="(min-width: 250px) 250px, calc(100vw - 40px)" data-srcset="https://www.history.com/.image/c_limit%2Ccs_srgb%2Cq_auto:good%2Cw_250/MTU3ODc4NjAwMDI5OTcxNzg1/image-placeholder-title.webp 250w"><source sizes="(min-width: 250px) 250px, calc(100vw - 40px)" data-srcset="https://www.history.com/.image/c_limit%2Ccs_srgb%2Cq_auto:good%2Cw_250/MTU3ODc4NjAwMDI5OTcxNzg1/image-placeholder-title.jpg 250w"><img class="m-detail--tml-image m-image" alt="A full-scale replica of Lucy&apos;s skull (Credit: Craig Hartley/Bloomberg via Getty Images)" decoding="async" src="https://www.history.com/.image/t_share/MTU3ODc4NjAwMDI5OTcxNzg1/image-placeholder-title.jpg" data-src="https://www.history.com/.image/c_limit%2Ccs_srgb%2Cfl_progressive%2Cq_auto:good%2Cw_700/MTU3ODc4NjAwMDI5OTcxNzg1/image-placeholder-title.jpg" height="300" width="250" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" itemprop="contentUrl url"></picture></a><div class="m-detail--tml-image-wrapper" style="max-width:250px; min-width:0px;"><div class="m-detail--tml-image-container" style="padding-top: 120%"><button class="m-social--pinterest-pin-it" class="tml-image--caption" itemprop="caption">A full-scale replica of Lucy&#x2019;s skull. (Credit: Craig Hartley/Bloomberg via Getty Images)</p></figcaption></figure></div><p>The new study supports the much-debated theory known as &#x201C;arborealism,&#x201D; according to which human ancestors lived partially in trees and partially on land. Given her small size, Lucy would have had to deal with predators like hyenas, saber-tooth cats and jackals, and the scientists believe she and her fellow early hominids took to the trees to protect themselves.</p><p>Other experts, however, say that the new study&#x2019;s authors didn&#x2019;t do enough to rule out other causes for the fractures in Lucy&#x2019;s bones. These critics include the paleoanthropologist Donald C. Johanson, who led the team that discovered Lucy&#x2019;s skeleton in 1974. Johanson told the New York Times that the fractures were far more likely to have occurred long after Lucy&#x2019;s death, as her bones were exposed to the elements and buried by sand. By the time Lucy lived, he contends, human ancestors were no longer skilled tree climbers, but had evolved to find their food on the ground. &#x201C;Australopithecus afarensis was essentially a terrestrial animal,&#x201D; Johanson <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2016/08/30/science/lucy-hominid-fossils-fall.html" rel="noopener" onclick="return phoenixTrackClickEvent(this, event);" target="_blank">said</a>.</p><p>Despite such criticism, there&#x2019;s no denying the intrigue surrounding a possible solution to such a famous cold case after more than 3 million years. Fortunately, armchair anthropologists will soon be able to judge for themselves, as the Ethiopian government has allowed Kappelman and his colleagues to publish their data online at <a href="https://elucy.org/" rel="noopener" onclick="return phoenixTrackClickEvent(this, event);" target="_blank">eLucy.org</a>.</p></div><div class="m-detail--blockthrough-ads"><span class="bt-uid-tg" uid="5b9a9071f7-168" style="display: none !important"></span></div><div class="m-detail--sponsor"></div><footer class="m-detail--footer"><div class="m-detail--meta"><dl><dt class="m-detail--label">Tags</dt><dt>terms:</dt><dd class="m-detail--keywords"><a href="/tag/early-humans">Early Humans</a></dd></dl></div><aside class="m-detail--author-box"><div class="m-detail--author-content"><div class="m-detail--author-byline"><div class="m-detail--author-byline-label">By</div> <a href="/author/sarah-pruitt" onclick="return phoenixTrackClickEvent(this, event);" phx-track-id="Author Name" rel="author">Sarah Pruitt</a></div><div class="m-detail--author-teaser"><p>Sarah Pruitt is a writer and editor based in seacoast New Hampshire. She has been a frequent contributor to History.com since 2005, and is the author of <em>Breaking History: Vanished! </em>(Lyons Press, 2017),<em> </em>which chronicles some of history's most famous disappearances.</p></div></div></aside><section class="m-social mm-social--below-content"><ul><li class="m-social--facebook"><a class="m-icon-button m-social--button" aria-label="facebook"
